Section 1:
April 25, 2025
Honorable Aaron Michlewitz, Chair
House Committee on Ways and Means
State House, Room 243
Boston, MA 02133
Honorable Michael J. Rodrigues, Chair
Senate Committee on Ways and Means
State House, Room 212
Boston, MA 02133
RE: Prior Year Deficiency Report—FY2025, Quarter 3
Dear Chair Michlewitz and Chair Rodrigues:
In accordance with Item 1599-2040 of Section 2B of Chapter 140 of the Acts of 2024, the Office of the
Comptroller hereby submits to the House and Senate Committees on Ways and Means the attached Paid
Prior Year Deficiency Report (the Report).
The Report contains information regarding payment of prior year deficiencies through chargebacks to
Fiscal Year 2025 funds.
Through the third quarter of Fiscal Year 2025, as detailed in the attached report, a total of
$20,969,235,69 was spent in prior year deficiencies for 47 departments. Of that amount, $5,199,429.50
was incurred in accounts that had sufficient funds (the department reverted funds to the General Fund at
the end of Fiscal Year 2024) and $15,769,806.19 was from accounts that had insufficient funds (the
department did not revert funds to the General Fund at the end of Fiscal Year 2024). Whether there
were sufficient or insufficient funds, the funding for prior year deficiencies is recouped from each
department’s current year appropriation.
Docusign Envel ope ID: BAA22C41-08E8-4E04-A5E8-3CEC20A5C82E
Prior Year Deficiency Report—FY2025, Quarter 3
April 25, 2025

If we can provide any additional information or respond to any questions, please let me know.
Sincerely,
William McNamara

Reason # of # of
Reason Short Description
Code Occurrences Depts
Billing dispute can take a lengthy time to settle. During the ongoing negotiation to resolve a dispute, the FY in which the
BD Billing Dispute 1 1
payment should have been made would be closed.
There are instances when vendor invoices are submitted after the close of the FY. There are several reasons, such as, the
LI vendor invoice was never sent, sent late or lost in the mail or the department did not recognize or reconcile outstanding Late Invoice 2,848 47
invoices before the close of the FY.
Unexpected bills are costs incurred by vendors on behalf of departments often to prevent business disruption. An example
would be malfunction/break of heating/cooling systems. Incidents such as this would require immediate
UB Unexpected Billing 0 0
repair/replacement without proper review of funding source. When such incidents occur the department usually, either
files a supplemental budget or will settle with a departmental PYD.
Misplaced/lost Invoices most often occurs with agencies that have regional offices. Vendors may ship their invoices to
MI regional offices for review and authorization. Regional offices then send the invoices to central office for payment. In Misplaced/lost Invoice 1 1
between the regional offices and the central office, bills could be lost or misplaced.
This type of error occurs when a department copies forward a PRC and the data entry person forgets to change the vendor
AE code from the PRC and submits the PRC to final. In this instance the wrong vendor will be paid. Unless the department Accounting Error 5 4
finds out before the end of the FY and pay the correct vendor, it would be required to process PYD.
There are specific instances where departments are required to provide services without the availability of sufficient funds.

invoices outstanding the PYD process may be used as well.

Honorable Michael J. Rodrigues, Chair

Boston, MA 02133
RE: Prior Year Deficiency Report—FY2025, Quarter 3
Dear Chair Michlewitz and Chair Rodrigues:
In accordance with Item 1599-2040 of Section 2B of Chapter 140 of the Acts of 2024, the Office of the
Comptroller hereby submits to the House and Senate Committees on Ways and Means the attached Paid
Prior Year Deficiency Report (the Report).
The Report contains information regarding payment of prior year deficiencies through chargebacks to
Fiscal Year 2025 funds.
Through the third quarter of Fiscal Year 2025, as detailed in the attached report, a total of
$20,969,235,69 was spent in prior year deficiencies for 47 departments. Of that amount, $5,199,429.50
was incurred in accounts that had sufficient funds (the department reverted funds to the General Fund at
the end of Fiscal Year 2024) and $15,769,806.19 was from accounts that had insufficient funds (the
department did not revert funds to the General Fund at the end of Fiscal Year 2024). Whether there
were sufficient or insufficient funds, the funding for prior year deficiencies is recouped from each
department’s current year appropriation.

If we can provide any additional information or respond to any questions, please let me know.

Reason # of # of
Reason Short Description
Code Occurrences Depts
Billing dispute can take a lengthy time to settle. During the ongoing negotiation to resolve a dispute, the FY in which the
BD Billing Dispute 1 1
payment should have been made would be closed.
There are instances when vendor invoices are submitted after the close of the FY. There are several reasons, such as, the
LI vendor invoice was never sent, sent late or lost in the mail or the department did not recognize or reconcile outstanding Late Invoice 2,848 47
invoices before the close of the FY.
Unexpected bills are costs incurred by vendors on behalf of departments often to prevent business disruption. An example
would be malfunction/break of heating/cooling systems. Incidents such as this would require immediate
UB Unexpected Billing 0 0
repair/replacement without proper review of funding source. When such incidents occur the department usually, either
files a supplemental budget or will settle with a departmental PYD.
Misplaced/lost Invoices most often occurs with agencies that have regional offices. Vendors may ship their invoices to
MI regional offices for review and authorization. Regional offices then send the invoices to central office for payment. In Misplaced/lost Invoice 1 1
between the regional offices and the central office, bills could be lost or misplaced.
This type of error occurs when a department copies forward a PRC and the data entry person forgets to change the vendor
AE code from the PRC and submits the PRC to final. In this instance the wrong vendor will be paid. Unless the department Accounting Error 5 4
finds out before the end of the FY and pay the correct vendor, it would be required to process PYD.
There are specific instances where departments are required to provide services without the availability of sufficient funds.
